  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c35195a3-3e87-4e1e-a242-de3308764d2f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer11909630983860969639">Tessa at sixteen, is pretty, but terribly shy and under-confident. Her best friend Matty is much more popular, not to mention more successful with boys. Tessa loves roaming the local parkland and often goes there for walks with the family dog. When developers threaten to destroy this, for the first time in her life Tessa decides to make a stand and joins a demonstration. T</span>
  <span id="freeText11909630983860969639" style="display:none">Tessa at sixteen, is pretty, but terribly shy and under-confident. Her best friend Matty is much more popular, not to mention more successful with boys. Tessa loves roaming the local parkland and often goes there for walks with the family dog. When developers threaten to destroy this, for the first time in her life Tessa decides to make a stand and joins a demonstration. There she meets Wolfie. She's seen him at school and he is well-known as a local activist. He is incredibly kind and helpful to her, and gradually as they find they have a lot in common, they fall deeply in love. Because Wolfie believes in her, Tessa's confidence grows and she finds herself supporting Matty and no longer hiding what she really feels. But just when things couldn't be working out better, tragedy strikes...</span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9782266169318" href="/book/show/7968696-tessa-in-love">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3737508-nicolle?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3737508-nicolle?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102991367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1014768507036704783"> Reading this book I went through all emotions known to man with Tessa. When she fell in love with Wolfie it was amazing to her, like feeling she had never felt before, but on recieveing the news thathe had died she felt devastated, and many of us who have lost someone we love can relate to this. I was crying at this point and felt an anger at the author, how could she do this to Wolfie. I had to remind myself that it was a book.<br/> The plot was well thought out and the charcters true to form. Over</span>
  <span id="freeText1014768507036704783" style="display:none"> Reading this book I went through all emotions known to man with Tessa. When she fell in love with Wolfie it was amazing to her, like feeling she had never felt before, but on recieveing the news thathe had died she felt devastated, and many of us who have lost someone we love can relate to this. I was crying at this point and felt an anger at the author, how could she do this to Wolfie. I had to remind myself that it was a book.<br /> The plot was well thought out and the charcters true to form. Overall making this book a pleasure to read. I could read this book again and again and still feel the shock that went through Tessa. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182053467" />
    <a title="Iona Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4480548-iona-sinclair"><img alt="Iona Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346604203p2/4480548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182053467?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iona Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iona Sinclair" href="/user/show/4480548-iona-sinclair">Iona Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11436700-tessa-in-love">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182053467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6194646064291874103">In many ways, i should have given this book five stars, but i just couldn't. I felt really close to the main character - Tessa - as her situation is similar to my own, and i found myself agreeing to most of what she was saying. Despite this, theres just something about this book that irritates me. The majority of the book was fine, but the ending seemed very sudden, and rushed, with the climax being told in about five words of direct speech. I felt that the book could have been slightly longer, </span>
  <span id="freeText6194646064291874103" style="display:none">In many ways, i should have given this book five stars, but i just couldn't. I felt really close to the main character - Tessa - as her situation is similar to my own, and i found myself agreeing to most of what she was saying. Despite this, theres just something about this book that irritates me. The majority of the book was fine, but the ending seemed very sudden, and rushed, with the climax being told in about five words of direct speech. I felt that the book could have been slightly longer, to allow time to explain what had happened better, and deliver it more imaginatively. Overall, though, worth reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6194646064291874103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText1020914095890914193" style="display:none"><i>'Love is the last thing we need right now, Tessa,’ Matty said.<br />As the credits rolled, we were both in a drippy, hopeless kind of state, having laughed at the cheesiness of the movie for as long as we could, and then fallen for it anyway. As usual.<br />‘But why?’ I said loudly, sounding a bit like I was going to burst into song. ‘I want it. And you’re in love anyway. It's a sweet love story between Tessa and Wolfie.<br /><br />Tessa has always been 'the quiet one', while her best friend, Matty, is outgoing and constantly has boys flocking around her. But when Tessa falls in love for the first time at sixteen, everything changes. She finds a soulmate in Wolfie, a committed green activist, and grows more confident and outspoken every day. She also begins to look at the world differently… everything seems better with Wolfie at her side.<br /><br />Tessa and Wolfie's romance is sweet, but sad - this is NOT a book with a happy ending, although the covers make it look like a frivolous YA novel. It's actually sweet, sad, and full of feeling. I'm glad I picked up this book, even though the ending made me very sad.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3586743141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3586743141" />
    <a title="Nicole Courtney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67704464-nicole-courtney"><img alt="Nicole Courtney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587741984p2/67704464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3586743141?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole Courtney" href="/user/show/67704464-nicole-courtney">Nicole Courtney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67704464-nicole-courtney?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3586743141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6150882033796707898">This book had an interesting idea and I wanted to try something different to what I usually read. I got this book via A Box of stories that you can subscribe to to save some books from being destroyed. It looked interesting and I thought it was going to be a light and easy read.<br/>Not the fault of the book, but the main character's love interest had the same name as a pet name I used for my ex. But I got past that. Where do I start thought?<br/>It was a bit awkward to read. With most books, you start re</span>
  <span id="freeText6150882033796707898" style="display:none">This book had an interesting idea and I wanted to try something different to what I usually read. I got this book via A Box of stories that you can subscribe to to save some books from being destroyed. It looked interesting and I thought it was going to be a light and easy read.<br />Not the fault of the book, but the main character's love interest had the same name as a pet name I used for my ex. But I got past that. Where do I start thought?<br />It was a bit awkward to read. With most books, you start reading and you speed up as you go through the pages but I could not do it with this one for some reason. The way it was written was awkward for me at least. I felt neutral about Tessa and it was nice that she acted like a teenager . As its from her person, it was nice that this character felt real to her age. She had some lovely interests which included her trying to save the local park ( ?? I think that is what it was??) and that she focused on other hobbies other than finding love. I imagine this read would be great for anyone who wants a short and simple ( but in no way bad) romance story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6150882033796707898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10744330917967810492">Thsi is the second book I've read by the Kate le Vann. I can't say the romance were as good as the first book I've read from her "Things I know about love", but it was really emotional at the end and once again she made me cry. It makes me wonder, can the author write stories that don't involve in heartbreakings ends?<br/>The similarity between the two books is that couples won't be together at the end. One of them (guy or girl) is somehow going to die, and leaving the other one behind to cope with h</span>
  <span id="freeText10744330917967810492" style="display:none">Thsi is the second book I've read by the Kate le Vann. I can't say the romance were as good as the first book I've read from her "Things I know about love", but it was really emotional at the end and once again she made me cry. It makes me wonder, can the author write stories that don't involve in heartbreakings ends?<br />The similarity between the two books is that couples won't be together at the end. One of them (guy or girl) is somehow going to die, and leaving the other one behind to cope with his/hers death.<br />Will we ever get happy endings in other of Kate's book?</span>
  <a data-text-id="10744330917967810492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dPe2Pd2eY8BBRBrcQqzBcHbj6cs8bFsRojXLLrItmmliQzMk1xVz+q040eVm3zEjGrWY+7jWOdYpw7mmO3pFuw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('702XvHmwXq308/OKEQZkZslknmKHHURNz+ahoRGKx3v5+RKlcztOlxiPOLM1dZQ1pTLvUgOnJopEENMpmN0YqQ==')})
  }
//]]>
